<item>
  <title><![CDATA[Web Application Firewalls]]></title>
  <link>https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/2021/09/18/web-application-firewalls/</link>
  <pubDate>Sat, 18 Sep 2021 11:33:34 +0000</pubDate>
  <dc:creator>kayimpex</dc:creator>
  <guid isPermaLink="false">https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/?p=704</guid>
  <description/>
  <content:encoded><![CDATA[<!-- wp:image {"align":"center","id":708,"width":397,"height":340,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/09/firewall-image.png?w=517" alt="" class="wp-image-708" width="397" height="340" /></figure></div>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Web application firewalls help monitor, filter and protect web applications from malicious attacks and unwanted internet traffic, including bots, injection and application-layer denial of service (DoS). </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The WAF will help you establish and manage rules for avoiding internet threats, includin&nbsp; cross-site scripting (XSS), SQL injection file inclusions, SQL injection, brute force attacks etc. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Web application firewall are deployed to protect web-facing applications and collect access logs for compliance, and analytics.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:more {"customText":"Continue Reading"} -->
<!--more Continue Reading-->
<!-- /wp:more -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Web application firewalls help protect business applications deployed in the public cloud, on-premises, and in multicloud environments with access controls based on geolocation data, whitelisted, and backlisted IP addresses, Hypertext Transfer Protocol Uniform Resource Locater (HTTP URL), and HTTP header. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>WAFs can identify and block malicious bot traffic with an advanced set of verification methods, inducing JavaScript, Completely Automated Public Turing Test to tell Computers and Humans Apart with CAPTCHAs, device interpreting, and human interaction algorithms. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>WAFs protect internet-facing applications from attacks as a result of integrated threat intelligence that aggregates from multiple sources and Open Web Application Security Project detection rules.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"fontSize":"medium"} -->
<p class="has-medium-font-size"><strong>Some of the tasks performed by Web Application Firewalls include:</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"fontSize":"normal"} -->
<p class="has-normal-font-size"><strong>Testing URLs:</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The WAF will look at the URL to spot anything out of the ordinary. That might consist of unexpected variables or the presence of SQL, indicating a potential injection attack.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"fontSize":"normal"} -->
<p class="has-normal-font-size"><strong>Filtering out spam traffic:</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Most WAFs will look for common spam keywords in the content that is being sent to the web application. Additional tests may be performed before the user is challenged or redirected away from the application.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"fontSize":"normal"} -->
<p class="has-normal-font-size"><strong>Blocking DDoS attacks:</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>WAFs can be used to prevent DDoS attacks by limiting the number of requests that IPs can make for a web application. Traffic is diverted or blocked before your web application can reach the point of failure. You can also filter and block access to protocols like FTP or SSH.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"fontSize":"normal"} -->
<p class="has-normal-font-size"><strong>Checking access to sensitive pages:</strong> </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>WAFs can double check the credentials of visitors before they are allowed to reach specific pages. They can use IP whitelists and blacklists to filter out illegitimate visitors in addition to other rules.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Remove potential XSS and SQL injection attacks:WAFs will check for the presence of code that is commonly used in Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) and SQL injection attacks.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"fontSize":"normal"} -->
<p class="has-normal-font-size"><strong>Malicious bot identification:</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>WAFs will look for common Internet bots that scan or attempt to exploit web applications, stopping them before they reach the application.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"fontSize":"normal"} -->
<p class="has-normal-font-size"><strong>Traffic filtering :</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>You can monitor and filter the traffic that is sent to your website application, diverting traffic based on special rules that you create.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Geolocation and IP intelligence:Visitors from specific hosts and regions can be identified and redirected.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"fontSize":"normal"} -->
<p class="has-normal-font-size"><strong>Analytics:</strong> </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Most WAFs will provide you with detailed analytics on the location and identity of visitors to your website application.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Web-application firewalls use deep packet inspection to address the limitations of network firewalls by applying rules at the HTTP layer. This means they are able to parse and analyze HTTP methods such as GET and POST, ensure the syntax of the traffic falls correctly within the protocol, and gives Web site operators the chance to block many Web-based attacks. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Web-application firewalls, like their network counterparts, may either monitor traffic and log anomalies or actively block inbound or outbound connections. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Inbound connections might be blocked if a parameter contains a pattern common to the cross-site scripting or SQL injection. Outbound connections might be blocked if the page's content appears to contain a database error message or match credit-card number patterns.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Configuring and tuning a Web-application firewall to your site takes time and effort guided by security personnel with knowledge of how the site works. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>However, even simple configurations can stop automated scans and security breaches taking place at a fundamental level.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->]]></content:encoded>

<item>
  <title><![CDATA[Open Source Software]]></title>
  <link>https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/2021/09/25/open-source-software/</link>
  <pubDate>Sat, 25 Sep 2021 12:08:08 +0000</pubDate>
  <dc:creator>kayimpex</dc:creator>
  <guid isPermaLink="false">https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/?p=715</guid>
  <description/>
  <content:encoded><![CDATA[<!-- wp:image {"align":"center","id":718,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/09/imageedit_2_6217686589.png?w=626" alt="" class="wp-image-718" /><figcaption>Open Source Software</figcaption></figure></div>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Open source software is code that is designed to be publicly accessibleanyone can see, modify, and distribute the code as they see fit.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Open source software is developed in a decentralized and collaborative way, relying on peer review and community production. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Open source software is often cheaper, more flexible, and has more longevity than its proprietary peers because it is developed by communities rather than a single author or company.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:more {"customText":"Continue Reading"} -->
<!--more Continue Reading-->
<!-- /wp:more -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Some cloud computing applications, like Google Apps, are proprietary. Others, like own Cloud and Next cloud, are open source.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Open source has become a movement and a way of working that reaches beyond software production. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The open source movement uses the values and decentralized production model of open source software to find new ways to solve problems in their communities and industries.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Linux for example is a free, open source operating system (OS), released under the GNU General Public License (GPL). Its also become the largest open source software project in the world.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Because Linux is released under an open source license, anyone can run, study, modify, and redistribute the source code, or even sell copies of their modified code, as long as they do so under the same license.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"fontSize":"large"} -->
<p class="has-large-font-size"><strong>5 benefits of Open Source Software for Your Business</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2>1. <strong>Control</strong></h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Many people prefer open source software because they have more control over that kind of software. They can examine the code to make sure it's not doing anything they don't want it to do, and they can change parts of it they don't like. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Users who aren't programmers also benefit from open source software, because they can use this software for any purpose they wishnot merely the way someone else thinks they should.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2>2. <strong>Training</strong></h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Other people like open source software because it helps them become better programmers. Because open source code is publicly accessible, anyone can easily study it as they learn to make better software.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>When people discover mistakes in programs' source code, they can share those mistakes with others to help them avoid making those same mistakes themselves.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2>3. <strong>Security</strong></h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Some people prefer open source software because they consider it more secure and stable than proprietary software. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Because anyone can view and modify open source software, someone might spot and correct errors or omissions that a program's original authors might have missed. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>And because so many programmers can work on a piece of open source software without asking for permission from original authors, they can fix, update, and upgrade open source software more quickly than they can proprietary software.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2>4. <strong>Stability </strong></h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Many users prefer open source software to proprietary software for important, long-term projects. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Because programmers publicly distribute the source code for open source software, users relying on that software for critical tasks can be sure their tools won't disappear or fall into disrepair if their original creators stop working on them. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Additionally, open source software tends to both incorporate and operate according to open standards.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2>5. <strong>Flexibility </strong></h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>After you make the investment in the proprietary software that you feel best suits your business, youre then locked into a system that is concrete, rigid, constantly needs upgrades and may contain unspecified bugs. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Open source programs keep an open code so you can constantly go in, rewrite the code so as your business changes and adapts, so will your software system.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->]]></content:encoded>

<item>
  <title><![CDATA[5 ways to power your Business with Cloud Services.]]></title>
  <link>https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/2021/10/04/5-ways-to-power-your-business-with-cloud-services/</link>
  <pubDate>Mon, 04 Oct 2021 07:05:30 +0000</pubDate>
  <dc:creator>kayimpex</dc:creator>
  <guid isPermaLink="false">https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/?p=722</guid>
  <description/>
  <content:encoded><![CDATA[<!-- wp:image {"align":"center","id":724,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none","className":"is-style-default"} -->
<div class="wp-block-image is-style-default"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/10/cloud-services-difference_network-coverage.jpg?w=1024" alt="Cloud Services" class="wp-image-724" /><figcaption>Cloud Services</figcaption></figure></div>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>If your company is like most growing organizations, youre are always on the lookout for simpler, more cost-effective ways to run IT.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>You might have heard that more and more businesses are achieving those results by turning to as-a-service, pay-as-you-go approaches for IT infrastructure.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>But you might have assumed that its a move that works best for larger companies.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:more {"customText":"Continue Reading"} -->
<!--more Continue Reading-->
<!-- /wp:more -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The reality is, these cloud-on-premises solutions can meet a large number of the challenges that midsized organizations face day in, day out.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p><strong>You dont have a lot of cash for upfront investments?&nbsp;</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p><a href="https://www.hpe.com/us/en/greenlake.html?altcid=sm_us-greenlake-lb">As-a-service</a> approaches enable you to get your projects up and running without them.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p><strong>Do you want to be able to cover unexpected upswings in demand without forking out for new boxes?&nbsp;</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>You can do that.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p><strong>Do you want to capitalize on digital transformation and get new services pushed out quickly to your customers  while reducing the ops burden on your IT folks by having experts run the solution?&nbsp;</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>This is a great way to do it.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>We have partnered with <a href="https://www.hpe.com/us/en/greenlake.html?altcid=sm_us-greenlake-lb">HPE GreenLake</a> for their flagship pay-per-use platform that delivers cloud services to wherever your apps and data live  from edge to colocation to data centre.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Its quick and easy to scale up or down as your needs change, and its managed for you by HPE. HPE GreenLake has been around for more than a decade now.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>But for years now <a href="https://www.kayimpex.com/">Kay Impex</a> has been working hard with HPE to make the benefits more accessible to midsize businesses.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Were very aware that smaller organizations have special requirements and different ways of doing things; for example, they often value the choice of working with a partner  something Ill come back to in a moment.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>HPE GreenLake is a powerful solution, right-sized to make your growing business faster and more agile while saving you money.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p><strong>As-a-service  everywhere</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>If youre not familiar with the consumption-based IT model, let us explain to you a bit more about how HPE GreenLake works. Our cloud services cover a huge range of workloads, including compute, networking, storage, SAP HANA, virtual desktop infrastructure, VMs, and a lot more.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>We can deliver the infrastructure in as few as 14 days. HPE metering technologies ensure that you pay only for the resources you consume, and a built-in buffer capacity enables you to handle both steady growth and unexpected increases in demand. HPE GreenLake also takes care of the operational side for you.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>You also get HPE GreenLake Central, a self-service platform that centralizes operations and insights across your entire estate  cloud as well as on-premises  giving you a unified view of usage, cost performance, compliance and more.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p><strong>5 big advantages that are not only for the big guys</strong></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Consider what this cloud services model could mean for your growing business You can:</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:list {"ordered":true} -->
<ol><li><strong>Do more while spending less upfront.</strong> HPE GreenLake gives you exceptional financial flexibility. You can sidestep big upfront expenditures, pay on a monthly bill, and easily expand capacity when you need it.<br><br>And were making it even easier with <a href="https://www.hpe.com/us/en/newsroom/press-release/2021/03/hewlett-packard-enterprise-drives-hybrid-cloud-disruption-with-new-hpe-greenlake-cloud-services-and-partnerships.html">the announcement today of three new modular HPE GreenLake cloud services</a> that provide low-cost, smaller entry points. You can start small; choose the deployment size, compute instance, or storage volume instances that best fit your needs; and scale incrementally.<br></li><li><strong>Simplify IT purchasing decisions and move faster.</strong> Enterprise IT departments are often vast, theyre buying stuff all the time, and they have the expertise to do a deep dive into every investment. If thats not you, however, you may not have that luxury. Every purchase counts, in a big way. With HPE GreenLake cloud services and valuable advice from our tech experts, you can access the latest technologies quickly and with minimum risk.<br><br>And when youre ready to make your move, you can bypass the all-too-familiar purchasing and deployment delays. You can get new services pushed out to your customers or end-users faster.<br></li><li><strong>Eliminate the management burden.</strong> Your teams will no longer have to strain to keep up with the latest knowledge for a vast range of new technologies. With the management services that are wrapped into every HPE GreenLake solution, you can free up talent to accelerate whats next for customers. You can focus on expanding your business, getting ahead of others in your space, and even competing with the big guys.<br></li><li><strong>Unlock the power of colocation.</strong> Many organizations prefer not to host a data centre on their premises  they prefer to get out of the business of managing infrastructure. Instead, they opt for a colocation facility so that their teams can focus more on business initiatives.<br><br>HPE GreenLake can bring all of the agility and flexibility of the cloud to this type of IT footprint. Joint customers can now run HPE GreenLake on CyrusOne or Equinix through one agreement and one invoice. This enables you to greatly simplify and accelerate your procurement process.</li></ol>
<!-- /wp:list -->

<!-- wp:list {"ordered":true,"start":5} -->
<ol start="5"><li><strong>Tap into the expertise of HPE partners</strong>. We understand that success is about much more than just the technology and that smaller organizations sometimes lack the in-house expertise to deploy the kind of innovative, game-changing technology that could strengthen their position in the marketplace.&nbsp;</li></ol>
<!-- /wp:list -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>You can access the expertise you need to ensure the success of your cloud services project through HPE Pointnext Services or our years of partnership with HPE. Its all about giving you choice.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>We understand that many growing businesses have come to rely on the experience and invaluable services they get from partners like us, as well as our advice on HPE solutions.</p>

<item>
  <title><![CDATA[Firewall Best practices to block ransomware]]></title>
  <link>https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/2021/10/11/firewall-best-practices-to-block-ransomware/</link>
  <pubDate>Mon, 11 Oct 2021 08:01:44 +0000</pubDate>
  <dc:creator>kayimpex</dc:creator>
  <guid isPermaLink="false">https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/?p=727</guid>
  <description/>
  <content:encoded><![CDATA[<!-- wp:image {"align":"center","id":753,"width":784,"height":362,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/10/network-firewall.png?w=650" alt="" class="wp-image-753" width="784" height="362" /></figure></div>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Ransomware continues to plague organizations, with over a third of companies surveyed across 30 countries revealing that they were hit by ransomware in the last year.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Such attacks are ever-increasing in complexity and adversaries are getting more efficient at exploiting network and system vulnerabilities, leaving organizations with a significant clean-up bill: a global average of an eye-watering US$1.85M - more than double the cost reported last year.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Modern firewalls are highly effective at defending against these types of attacks, but they need to be given the chance to do their job.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Lets discuss how these attacks work, how they can be stopped, and best practices for configuring your firewall and network to give you the best protection possible.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:more {"customText":"Continue Reading"} -->
<!--more Continue Reading-->
<!-- /wp:more -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2><strong>Who hackers are targeting ?</strong></h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The short answer: everyone.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>In a recent survey of 5,400 mid-sized organizations across 30 countries, 37% of respondents said they had been hit by ransomware in the last year. No country, sector or vertical segment is safe.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:image {"align":"center","id":732,"width":564,"height":330,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/10/untitled-design-2.png?w=1024" alt="" class="wp-image-732" width="564" height="330" /><figcaption>In the last year, has your organization been hit by ransomware? Yes [base numbers in chart] omitting some answer options, split by sector</figcaption></figure></div>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>If you search the news for ransomware attack you will find several new successful attacks occurring every week. The effects are devastating: huge ransomware demands, significant downtime and business disruption, reputation damage, loss of data, and in an increasing number of cases, sensitive company data are being auctioned off by attackers.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2>How do ransomware attacks get on the network?</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Ransomware actors use a wide range of Tactics, Techniques and Procedures (TTP) to penetrate their victims' networks. Our experts have seen an increase in attacks where adversaries try multiple approaches until they find the chink in the organization's defences..</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:image {"align":"center","id":737,"width":597,"height":336,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/10/untitled-design-1.png?w=1024" alt="" class="wp-image-737" width="597" height="336" /><figcaption>How did the ransomware attack get into your organization? Question asked to respondents whose organization had been hit by ransomware in the last year. Base: 2,538 respondents.</figcaption></figure></div>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The top entry point for ransomware is through files downloaded or sent to users in spam or phishing attacks.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Dont leave security in the hands of your users. For these types of attacks, its best to safeguard your organization with strong firewall protection.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2>How do ransomware attack work</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:list {"ordered":true} -->
<ol><li><strong>Gain Entry:</strong> Spam or phishing email with a malicious attachment, or a web download or document containing exploits. Remote file-sharing /management features such as RDP.</li></ol>
<!-- /wp:list -->

<!-- wp:list {"ordered":true,"start":2} -->
<ol start="2"><li><strong>Escalate privileges until they are an administrator:</strong> Attackers exploit system vulnerabilities to gain privilege levels that let them bypass security software. They may restart and run the compromised host in Safe Mode to do this.</li></ol>
<!-- /wp:list -->

<!-- wp:list {"ordered":true,"start":3} -->
<ol start="3"><li><strong>Attempt to disable/bypass security software using highly-tailored files:</strong> Failing this, they will attempt to breach the security management console and disable the security system.</li></ol>
<!-- /wp:list -->

<!-- wp:list {"ordered":true,"start":4} -->
<ol start="4"><li><strong>Deploy payload</strong>: Using an automated exploit Manual network reconnaissance will first look for backups stored on the local network and delete them; making recovery much more difficult and increasing the chances of the victim paying the ransom. They then often exfiltrate sensitive company data for sale on the dark web.</li></ol>
<!-- /wp:list -->

<!-- wp:list {"ordered":true,"start":5} -->
<ol start="5"><li><strong>Spread ransomware</strong>: Hackers will then encrypt the organizations data and files utilizing a network and host vulnerabilities or basic file sharing protocols to compromise other systems on the network and spread file-encrypting ransomware.</li></ol>
<!-- /wp:list -->

<!-- wp:list {"ordered":true,"start":6} -->
<ol start="6"><li><strong>Leave a ransom note demanding payment for files to be decrypted.</strong></li><li><strong>Wait for the victim to contact them via email or a dark web website.</strong></li></ol>
<!-- /wp:list -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2>Remote Desktop Protocol or Ransomware Deployment Protocol</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Remote Desktop Protocol (RDP) and other desktop sharing tools like Virtual Network Computing (VNC) are innocuous and highly useful features of most operating systems that allow staff to access and manage systems remotely.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Unfortunately, without the proper safeguards in place, they also provide convenient in-roads for attackers and are commonly exploited by targeted ransomware.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Not properly securing RDP and other similar remote management protocols behind a Virtual Private Network (VPN) or at least restricting which IP addresses can connect via remote tools can leave you wide open to attackers.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Attackers often use brute-force hacking tools which try hundreds of thousands of username and password combinations until they get the right one.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2>How to stay protected from ransomware</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>To properly protect your organization from ransomware, there are three major initiatives you should undertake.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p><strong>Upgrade your IT security:</strong> Your firewall and endpoint security can protect against attacks getting onto the network in the first place, and if an attack should somehow penetrate your network, they can prevent it from spreading and infecting other systems. But not all firewalls and endpoint security solutions can do this effectively, so make sure you have an IT security system that does. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Ensure you have:</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:list -->
<ul><li>Affordable sandboxing to analyze file behaviour as its run before it gets on your network.</li><li>The latest machine learning technology to identify new zero-day variants in any files coming through the firewall.</li><li>Firewall IPS with live signature updating to block network exploits.</li><li>Free and easy remote access VPN to enable management of your network remotely without compromising on security.</li><li>Endpoint protection with anti-ransomware capabilities.</li></ul>
<!-- /wp:list -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p><strong>Lockdown remote access and management:</strong> When it comes to networks, every opening to the outside world is a potential vulnerability waiting to be exploited by a ransomware attack. Locking down your organizations Remote Desktop Protocol access, open ports, and other management protocols are one of the most effective steps you can take to secure against targeted ransomware attacks.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>There are numerous ways you can do this. One popular method is to require all users to be on a VPN before they can access resources such as RDP and restrict VPN access to known IP addresses. Also, properly secure and harden your servers, use complex passwords that are changed frequently, and leverage multi-factor authentication.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p><strong>Segment your network:</strong> Unfortunately, many organizations operate with a flat network topology: all of their endpoints connect into a common switch fabric. This topology compromises protection by enabling easy lateral movement or propagation of attacks within the local network since the firewall has no visibility or control over the traffic flowing through the switch.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:image {"align":"center","id":747,"width":648,"height":364,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/10/untitled-design-3.png?w=1024" alt="" class="wp-image-747" width="648" height="364" /></figure></div>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>A best practice is to segment the LAN into smaller subnets using zones or VLANs and then connecting these through the firewall to enable the application of anti-malware and IPS protection between segments. This can effectively identify and block threats attempting to move laterally on the network.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:image {"align":"center","id":750,"width":638,"height":359,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/10/untitled-design-4.png?w=1024" alt="" class="wp-image-750" width="638" height="359" /></figure></div>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Whether you use zones or VLANs depends on your network segmentation strategy and scope, but both offer similar security capabilities by providing the option to apply suitable security and control over traffic movement between segments.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Zones are ideal for smaller segmentation strategies or networks with unmanaged switches. VLANs are the preferred method for segmenting internal networks in most cases and offer the ultimate flexibility and scalability.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>However, they require the use (and configuration) of managed Layer 3 switches.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>While its a best practice to segment your network, theres no best way to segment a network. You can segment your network by user type (internal, contractors, guests), by department (sales, marketing, engineering), by service, device, or role type (VoIP, Wi-Fi, IoT, computers, servers) or any combination that makes sense for your network architecture.&nbsp;</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>But generally, youll want to segment less trusted and more vulnerable parts of your network from the rest. Youll also want to segment large networks into smaller segments, all to reduce the risk of threat penetration and propagation.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->]]></content:encoded>

<item>
  <title><![CDATA[Six predictions for the future of the edge]]></title>
  <link>https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/2021/11/24/six-predictions-for-the-future-of-the-edge/</link>
  <pubDate>Wed, 24 Nov 2021 07:04:00 +0000</pubDate>
  <dc:creator>kayimpex</dc:creator>
  <guid isPermaLink="false">https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/?p=757</guid>
  <description/>
  <content:encoded><![CDATA[<!-- wp:image {"id":766,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<figure class="wp-block-image size-large"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/11/image-23.jpg?w=865" alt="" class="wp-image-766" /></figure>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The edge is going to change the way we interact with each other and the world.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Thanks to edge computing, the world is about to look much different.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Within a decade, the edge will boast more computing powerand produce far more datathan the cloud does today, says Lin Nease, HPE Fellow and chief technologist for IoT.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The edge is where the Internet of Things, artificial intelligence, and ultrafast 5G networks are converging. And that will change our lives dramatically over the next few years.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Here are six major trends we can expect to see over the coming decade.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:more {"customText":"Continue Reading"} -->
<!--more Continue Reading-->
<!-- /wp:more -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="1-every-large-facility-will-have-its-own-edge-data-center">1. Every large facility will have its own edge data center.</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>By the year 2025, the number of connected devices in the wild is expected to exceed&nbsp;56 billion, according to IDC. And as IoT sensors proliferate through public and private spaces, the volume of data they produce will grow exponentially.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Organizations will need to process that data locally so they can act on it in real-time, Nease says. Instead of shuttling that data to the cloud, they'll be operating their own mini data centres on-site. Modular, self-contained units like&nbsp;the HPE Edge Center, which can be placed wherever needed, will become common across a wide range of industries.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"Within three years, all operations facilities, including retail stores, hospitals, warehousesany place the physical operations of the company occurwill have data room capabilities to ingest data from cameras, microphones, and environmental sensors," says Nease. "These little edge clouds will resemble the private clouds companies already have in their big data centres, but with less than a dozen servers."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>And instead of deploying increasingly intelligent end devices, many organizations will opt for inexpensive sensors that simply collect data, which is then processed locally in their small private clouds.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"The low-cost approach is to buy cheap sensors and have software running somewhere in the facility that can do pattern recognition or infrared sensing," Nease says. "If you're a large retailer, for example, you will do this in your store in about three years. You will have to if you want to compete."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="2-smarter-spaces-will-enable-frictionless-transactions">2. Smarter spaces will enable frictionless transactions</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Data captured by edge devices in public spaces will help provide context around who people are and what they came there to do. That will change both how these spaces are designed and how people interact with them, says Partha Narasimhan, CTO at Aruba, a Hewlett Packard Enterprise company.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"Today, some of the contexts is split between the digital world and the physical world," he says. "Those two will absolutely come together."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>For example, when you walk into your bank, smart cameras can identify you as a regular customer and make an intelligent guess as to why you came in, says Narasimhan. If you were researching interest rates on the bank's website the night before, a loan officer could be expecting you, with your financial records already called up on the screen.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Similarly, when you step into your doctor's waiting room, edge systems can automatically check you in, pull up your electronic medical record, take your copayment, and alert the nurse you've arrived.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"As you journey through your course of care, hospitals will know who you are, where you are, and what assets, like wheelchairs or X-ray machines, you are using," notes Christian Renaud, research director for IoT at 451 Research. "They'll have lower operational costs, you'll have a faster diagnostic experience, and clinicians will get to spend more time with patients and less time entering data into electronic health records."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>And, as we gradually return to the workplace, edge systems in the building will know that we're there primarily to collaborate with colleagues. We may be assigned a different workspace each day, depending on the people we need to collaborate with that day. Offices will be redesigned with more meeting rooms and fewer cubicles, better teleconferencing gear, smarter whiteboards, and more ways to intelligently capture the content of conversations.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"To some people, it may feel a little creepy that someone already knows who you are and why you're there," says Narasimhan. "But so long as you manage that data in a secure way that respects people's privacy, most of us will overcome that feeling because it's so convenient."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="3-the-robots-will-be-watching-us-and-learning">3. The robots will be watching usand learning</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The killer app for AI-powered cameras at the edge won't be security surveillance or autonomous vehicles, Nease says. Instead, they will be helping many of us become better at our jobs.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"People will be analyzing the physical environment of their operations using computer vision," he says. "But instead of employing it as a management tool, they'll be using it to redesign processes to figure out how to make them more efficient."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Companies like&nbsp;Drishti&nbsp;are already doing this on manual assembly lines for companies like Ford and Honeywell, using smart cameras to quantify processes, identify quality control issues, and train employees more effectively.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>A major luxury carmaker is studying how to use computer vision and robots to mimic the work of its craftspeople, notes Dr Eng Lim Goh, CTO for high-performance computing and artificial intelligence at HPE. The goal is not to replace human workers but to enable the creation of highly customized bespoke vehicles, built to the exact requirements of each customer.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"These robots will not only learn from humans but also from each other," he says. "And if you have factories in different countries, they'll be able to share their learnings across borders."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="4-edge-devices-will-begin-to-learn-on-their-own">4. Edge devices will begin to learn on their own</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Today, edge devices infer decisions based on machine learning models that have been trained in the cloud and then pushed down to the edge. But as the battery life of IoT devices improves and their computing power increases, these devices will begin to learn on their own, Goh says.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"The beauty of this is that the devices collect the data and then immediately learn from it," he adds. "Imagine the latency reduction in your decision-making."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>To avoid bias that can be introduced by relying on limited sets of training data, edge devices will be able&nbsp;to learn from and analyze data from multiple sensors, a concept known as&nbsp;swarm learning. Because devices share only the insights gleaned from the data, the data itself remains private and secure, Goh adds.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>For example, connected X-ray machines at a hospital that treats a lot of patients with tuberculosis can share insights with another location that sees more cases of pneumonia. The ability to analyze lung X-rays at both facilities improves, while no patient data is shared.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"We'll continue to see more robust compute and analytics get further and further out in the network until they approach the point of origination, whether that's a camera, a sensor, a drill press, or an MRI machine," Renaud says.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="5-augmented-and-virtual-reality-will-become-actual-realities">5. Augmented and virtual reality will become actual realities</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Today's AR and VR apps have proved how quickly nascent consumer technologies can deliver value in enterprise settings. As edge compute and connectivity continue to advance, we will see a continued evolution of experiences that are more immersive, with equipment that is less intrusive. That will drive continued applications of AR and VR into use cases that today are considered impractical.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>With greater compute and storage capability at the edge, images and video can be cached locally and served up instantly via ultra-low-latency 5G networks.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"The edge will enable new services like AR and VR that require content to be closer to where users are," says Narasimhan. "Virtual experiences will be enhanced to the point where they're easy and intuitive to consume. And as they get more refined, they will make it easier for people to meet virtually."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Beyond reducing the need for business travel, AR and VR will be deployed in a wide range of&nbsp;industrial and commercial settings&nbsp;to improve workflows, bridge expertise supply and demand imbalances, and transform customer experiences.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Factory workers can use AR glasses to view 3D schematics as they assemble parts. AR mirrors inside&nbsp;clothing stores&nbsp;will let customers digitally try on different outfits. We will see more widespread use of the technology by doctors to&nbsp;perform remote surgery&nbsp;a thousand miles away from the operating theatre. Visitors to&nbsp;theme parks&nbsp;will use it to interact with life-size holograms of their favourite characters.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"AR will allow employees to play with different datasets and explore them from different perspectives," notes Ross Rubin, principal analyst at Reticle Research. "It will be useful for any application that frees people from having to look at a screen at a particular time and overlay information in a way that sparks insights that might not otherwise be available in that environment."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="6-the-big-privacy-issues-will-eventually-be-solved">6. The big privacy issues will eventually be solved</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The ability to deliver digital services to anyone in any location carries with it the ability to track everyone's behaviour everywhere. Organizations that hope to realize the full benefits of edge computing will need to solve the privacy problem.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"We've done more than 50 consumer and enterprise surveys over the past five years, and privacy always comes up as one of the top concerns," Renaud says. "Hopefully, enlightened regulation will moderate the ambitious potential of the technology to get to a point where our privacy is safe."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>In the European Union, for example, data sovereignty rules limit the physical locations where information can be stored, and some countries require connected cameras to automatically blur faces or license plate numbers.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Technologies like swarm learning, which allows insights to be shared without needing the underlying data, can help alleviate data sovereignty concerns. HPE and others are currently working on new data standards that would allow people greater control over how their data is used, Nease says.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"I think these standards will emerge and people will give permission for their data to be used, just as they do with Google every time they perform a search," he says. "But there is no stopping the privacy problem. It is now upon us."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="3-the-robots-will-be-watching-us-and-learning"><br></h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->]]></content:encoded>

<item>
  <title><![CDATA[AR and VR: From gaming novelty to enterprise essential]]></title>
  <link>https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/2021/11/25/ar-and-vr-from-gaming-novelty-to-enterprise-essential/</link>
  <pubDate>Thu, 25 Nov 2021 09:31:28 +0000</pubDate>
  <dc:creator>kayimpex</dc:creator>
  <guid isPermaLink="false">https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/?p=769</guid>
  <description/>
  <content:encoded><![CDATA[<!-- wp:image {"id":778,"width":771,"height":416,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<figure class="wp-block-image size-large is-resized"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/11/image-25.jpg?w=541" alt="" class="wp-image-778" width="771" height="416" /></figure>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Advances in hardware and software, infrastructure, and other technologies are driving greater use of virtual, augmented, and mixed realities for both work and play, laying the foundation for what experts call the human edge.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Augmented and virtual reality has been around for some time, but only more recently have they begun to push the boundaries of how we work and play. With the ever-evolving capabilities of our smartphones and advances in hardware and software, network infrastructure, and other technologies, AR and VR are at a tipping point, moving beyond gaming and entertainment toward mainstream use.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:more {"customText":"Continue Reading"} -->
<!--more Continue Reading-->
<!-- /wp:more -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>In fact, these developments, along with emerging mixed reality (MR) and extended reality (XR) technologies, could soon change how we interact with each other and the world on a day-to-day basisessentially creating the "human edge."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>In this episode of Technology Untangled, hostMichael Birdand guests explore the evolution of AR and VR, real-world applications today, and what an augmented future might look like.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="why-vr-now">Why VR now?</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>According toMatt Armstrong-Barnes, chief technologist at Hewlett Packard Enterprise, two things have been holding back VR adoption: cost and the size of headsets and other equipment. But that's changing.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"The cost of obtaining the equipment required to run a virtual environment is coming down significantly," he says. And while there are limits to how small headsets can get due to the way human eyes have to interact with screens, VR gear is becoming increasingly smallerand often as devices shrink in size, they become cheaper, he adds.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>With the rollout of 5G networks, other barriersnamely latency and lack of bandwidthare disappearing too, says Leslie Shannon, head of ecosystem and scouting at Nokia.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"[5G] connects that minimum processing chip on the end device to servers sitting at the network edge," she explains. "And so what this does is it gives you a better end device in terms of cost and scalability and heat generation and being something light that you might want to wear on your head while pairing it with far more powerful computing power than is available in the single chips that are in devices today."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="where-vr-stands-today">Where VR stands today</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Current VR options include headsets like Oculus Quest for mobile use and Microsoft HoloLens for primarily industrial settings, along with larger devices like the Valve Index, which is "the gold standard of VR at the moment," saysAlex Haddock, HPE's chief technologist for hybrid IT, retail, and MDI. As for AR and MR, he adds, we've already got powerful devices for those experiences in our pockets: smartphones.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"Google AR is a very exciting thing," saysLauren Dyer, director of strategic partnerships at Dimension Studio. And with social media platforms now offering immersive experiences, "it doesn't feel like a barrier to entry anymore," she adds. "A lot of it now is web-powered, and we've really seen that transformation in the last 24 months."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Of course, gaming and entertainment are where virtual and other realities continue to make stridesfrom mobile AR apps like Pokemon Go to virtual studios that bring together people from around the world for coverage of sporting and other events.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"We're seeing quite a lot of inquiries from broadcasters wanting to create [virtual studios] purely because it enables the fans to be closer to the action," Dyer says. "It also enables the people doing the shows at the time to have a lot more control of the space. And most importantly, it just looks really great. It looks really slick."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>In business, marketers are increasingly using VR and other realities to make products come to lifeliterally. For example, Dyer describes a mixed reality H&amp;M marketing campaign her company created where consumers around the globe could scan a QR code to experience AR character performances featuring the retailer's fashion right on their devices.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"[AR] has been a great way of engaging and creating participation," she says. "And when you add a layer of interactivity to it, it becomes a lot more exciting, and the entertainment value of it is not just being a gimmick but it's allowing that invaluable and memorable moment with the consumer and the brands."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="a-vr-future">A VR future</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Beyond entertainment and selling products and services, AR, VR, and MR are bringing big improvements to fields like medicine and maintenance and repairs.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"I think the opportunities are boundless," Haddock says. He highlights surgery as an example, whereby general surgeons in remote hospitals who need guidance on a particular procedure can implement mixed reality technologies to tap the expertise of other surgeons thousands of miles away.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>In maintenance and repair fields, "you have that capability for someone to go to a site and visualize the blueprints of where things should be in front of their eyes," he says.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Other advances, beyond improvements in hardware and infrastructure, are on the horizon. As Haddock notes,artificial intelligence,neuromorphic computing, andswarm learningwill soon take AR, VR, MR, and XR to new levels, essentially creating "the human edge."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"[It] boils down to how we get that visual input  whether it's initially lenses that project it or perhaps something that beams onto your eye, or ultimately, something that does it directly into your brain. I mean, who knows? I think it's just going to grow and grow," Haddock says.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"It will be ubiquitous. It won't be something that distracts us," he adds. "We just put it on in the morning, whatever format that might be, or integrate it. And it will be everything from concerts to work."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->]]></content:encoded>

<item>
  <title><![CDATA[Semiconductors]]></title>
  <link>https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/2021/12/04/it-simplified-semiconductor/</link>
  <pubDate>Sat, 04 Dec 2021 10:56:34 +0000</pubDate>
  <dc:creator>kayimpex</dc:creator>
  <guid isPermaLink="false">https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/?p=802</guid>
  <description/>
  <content:encoded><![CDATA[<!-- wp:gallery {"linkTo":"none"} -->
<figure class="wp-block-gallery has-nested-images columns-default is-cropped"><!-- wp:image {"id":823,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<figure class="wp-block-image size-large"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/12/352_roland_berger_chip_shortage_in_the_automotive_industry_it_image_caption_none.webp?w=768" alt="" class="wp-image-823" /></figure>
<!-- /wp:image --></figure>
<!-- /wp:gallery -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"ampFitText":true} -->
<amp-fit-text layout="fixed-height" min-font-size="6" max-font-size="72" height="80"><p>A semiconductor is a computer chip that serves as the brain of anything that's computerized or uses radio waves. It handles complex thinking such as arithmetic and data storage that is integral to cell phones, tablets, kitchen gadgets, laptops, video game consoles and automobiles.</p></amp-fit-text>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"ampFitText":true} -->
<amp-fit-text layout="fixed-height" min-font-size="6" max-font-size="72" height="80"><p> In vehicles, dozens of individual semiconductor chips are used to control everything from engine temperature to alert drivers of the need for an oil change. The types of chips produced by semiconductor companies can be categorized in two ways(As per the integrated circuits or functionality of the chip). </p></amp-fit-text>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Usually, chips are categorized in terms of their functionality. However, they are sometimes divided into types according to the integrated circuits (ICs) used.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:more -->
<!--more-->
<!-- /wp:more -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>When looked at according to functionality, the four main categories of semiconductors are memory chips, microprocessors, standard chips and complex systems-on-a-chip (SoCs). When organized by types of integrated circuitry, the three types of chips are digital, analogue and mixed.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"ampFitText":true} -->
<amp-fit-text layout="fixed-height" min-font-size="6" max-font-size="72" height="80"><p>Semiconductors are materials that have electrical conductivity between conductors (generally metals) and nonconductors or insulators (such as most ceramics). Most chips are groups of numerous transistors, diodes, resistors and capacitors which are a part of an integrated circuit, and are connected to each other seamlessly. </p></amp-fit-text>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"ampFitText":true} -->
<amp-fit-text layout="fixed-height" min-font-size="6" max-font-size="72" height="80"><p>These components respectively play different roles in processing and storing electric signals that run the software, manipulate data and control the functions of electronic devices. The arrangement of those circuits gives them their specific purpose.</p></amp-fit-text>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:image {"id":807,"width":771,"height":416,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<figure class="wp-block-image size-large is-resized"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/12/image0.jpeg?w=1024" alt="" class="wp-image-807" width="771" height="416" /><figcaption><em>Nvidia GPU used for converting computer code into realistic video game graphics</em></figcaption></figure>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"ampFitText":true} -->
<amp-fit-text layout="fixed-height" min-font-size="6" max-font-size="72" height="80"><p>The three biggest chip companies in the world in 2020 were Taiwan Semiconductor Manufacturing Co&nbsp; Samsung and Intel. Chip companies try to pack more transistors into chips, enhancing performance and making devices more power-efficient. </p></amp-fit-text>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Intels was the leader in manufacturing chips from the 80s to 2000 since the first microprocessorthe 4004was released in 1971 and contained only 2,300 transistors with a node size of 10 microns or 10 millionths of a meter. Intels undisputed leadership of the previous decades ended between 2015 and 2020 when rivals Taiwan Semiconductor Manufacturing Co. and Samsung Electronics Co. started building chips with better transistors: ones with dimensions down to 5 nanometers.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"ampFitText":true} -->
<amp-fit-text layout="fixed-height" min-font-size="6" max-font-size="72" height="80"><p>Chips consist of as many as 100 layers of materials. These are deposited, then partially removed, to form complex three-dimensional structures that connect all the tiny transistors. Some of these layers are just one atom thin. One of the key components is siliconor purified sandand the magic happens in how it is processed and manipulated. Before you put silicon into chipmaking machines, you need a cleanroom.</p></amp-fit-text>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"ampFitText":true} -->
<amp-fit-text layout="fixed-height" min-font-size="6" max-font-size="72" height="80"><p>Individual transistors are many times smaller than a virus. Just one speck of dust can cause havoc and millions of dollars of wasted effort. To mitigate this risk, chipmakers house their machines in rooms that essentially have no dust. To maintain that environment, the air is constantly filtered and very few people are allowed in.</p></amp-fit-text>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"ampFitText":true} -->
<amp-fit-text layout="fixed-height" min-font-size="6" max-font-size="72" height="80"><p>Setting up semiconductor manufacturing plants otherwise known as foundries is unbelievably complex and specialized with limited companies operating in only a few geographical regions. A semiconductor fabrication plant is where integrated circuits (ICs), also known as microchips, are manufactured. </p></amp-fit-text>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"ampFitText":true} -->
<amp-fit-text layout="fixed-height" min-font-size="6" max-font-size="72" height="80"><p>They are either operated by Integrated Device Manufacturers (IDMs) who design and manufacture ICs in-house and may also manufacture designs from design-only (known as fabless firms which outsource the manufacturing of these chips), or by Pure Play foundries, that manufacture designs from fabless companies and do not design their own ICs. Some Pure Play foundries like Samsung, design and manufacture ICs for customers, while also designing, manufacturing and selling their own ICs.</p></amp-fit-text>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph {"ampFitText":true} -->
<amp-fit-text layout="fixed-height" min-font-size="6" max-font-size="72" height="80"><p></p></amp-fit-text>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->]]></content:encoded>

<item>
  <title><![CDATA[The fundamentals of security incident responseduring a pandemic and beyond]]></title>
  <link>https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/2021/12/16/the-fundamentals-of-security-incident-response-during-a-pandemic-and-beyond/</link>
  <pubDate>Thu, 16 Dec 2021 10:55:30 +0000</pubDate>
  <dc:creator>kayimpex</dc:creator>
  <guid isPermaLink="false">https://kayimpex.wordpress.com/?p=827</guid>
  <description/>
  <content:encoded><![CDATA[<!-- wp:image {"id":831,"sizeSlug":"large","linkDestination":"none"} -->
<figure class="wp-block-image size-large"><img src="https://kayimpex.files.wordpress.com/2021/12/si-catagory-incidentresponse402x.jpg?w=1024" alt="" class="wp-image-831" /></figure>
<!-- /wp:image -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Information security is a nonstop race between you and cybercriminalsand COVID-19 means more challenges for your organization and more opportunities for attackers. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>We spoke with cybersecurity experts about the challenges a new remote workforce creates for organizations, how to respond to a cyber threat, and how the threats themselves are changing.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:more {"customText":"Continue Reading"} -->
<!--more Continue Reading-->
<!-- /wp:more -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The ongoing COVID-19 pandemic makes it more difficult to respond to a threat in progress. Being proactive is crucial, and the best time to update your strategy to reflect a shelter-in-place workforce is the same for every business, large or small: yesterday.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="what-s-at-stake">What's at stake?</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Breaches come in different sizes and scales. Ransomware can keep you from resources and data, but the game plan is very different depending on what's compromisedand what that infected point has touched. The solution to a workstation encrypted by a ransomware attack can be straightforward: rebuild the machine, which means downtime but not much else. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>However, if a data centre or critical servers are compromised, the results could be catastrophic. For many companies, the potential loss is so great that sending hundreds of thousands of dollars in cryptocurrency to cybercriminals makes senseeven when paying the ransom is just the start of your headache.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"Even if you can find a way to pay, can afford to pay, and have a trustworthy enough criminal ... it still doesn't mean you're going to survive the attack," says Drew Simonis, deputy chief information security officer at HPE. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Even if you pay a ransom, repairing the damage from a ransomware attack with security keys provided by a criminal can still mean months of downtime. How much-lost productivity can your organization survive? "For a large company, it may be sustainable," says Simonis. "For a small company? That could put them out of business."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="the-five-pillars-of-cybersecurity">The five pillars of cybersecurity</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Obviously, the kinds of attacks you face and the resources at your disposal depending on the size of your organization. But the crucial actions you must take are drawn from the National Institute of Standards and Technology's (NIST) cybersecurity framework, and they are the same for businesses big and small: identity, protect, detect, respond, and recover. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>It's a step-by-step process for assessing how vulnerable your system is, doing everything you can to remove vulnerabilities, quickly triaging the damage when a breach does occur, getting up and running again, andmost importanteradicating those weak links for the future.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Not all organizations are created equal. "A big company has all those resources in-house; they'll have the investigators, the forensic capability, the ability to develop a plan based on the breach and put that plan into action," says Simonis. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Response plans differ depending on size and budget, and many of the challenges that small and midsize businesses face are more daunting than ever due to the ongoing pandemic.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="the-covid-factor">The COVID factor</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>A growing remote workforce makes every step of response harder. The COVID-19 pandemic hasn't changed the fundamentals, but it has created new opportunities for cybercriminals: an uptick in content-oriented attacks that target the people in your organizationespecially with emotional pleas. In April, the World Health Organization reported dealing with&nbsp;<em>five times&nbsp;</em>more cyber attacks than usual.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"Security teams have to learn to sift through what they didn't have to sift through before," says J.J. Thompson, senior director of managed threat response at Sophos.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Google's Threat Analysis Group warns that phishing attacks directed at the general public are masquerading as government services. "In a post-pandemic world, it's [still] going to be email and communication boards, social engineering attacks ... [but] they're going to have a much better uptake rate." </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>COVID-19-related attackslike phishing attempts disguised as COVID test resultsare particularly dangerous. "We all have a more porous social engineering filter than we had before," the group says.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The challenges brought to light by the pandemic may not even be newand they certainly aren't going anywhere. "What you have to be able to deal with is an environment in which you can't trust messaging that originates from outside your organization. Any time someone from the outside asks you to do something, you should be suspicious," says HPE's Simonis. He suggests verifying unusual requests as much as possibleeven if it means making a phone call.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Eliminating human vulnerabilities also means building systems that are prepared for the inevitability that people will make mistakes. "Assume all of those procedures are going to fail," says Thompson. "No matter how many times you train somebody not to click on something, they're going to do it anyway." </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>The key is to put tools in place that pick up where people fail, like identifying anonymous logins, even if a user's credentials check out.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="what-you-can-do-today">What you can do today</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Even meticulous backups are no substitute for a sophisticated incident response plan. Some breaches can't be fixed by just reverting to a backup. "Almost all ransomware waits three days to get through two or three backup cycles&nbsp;<em>before&nbsp;</em>they actually ask for the money," says Gary Campbell, security chief technology officer at HPE. And your backups may not be enough to prevent potentially lethal damage. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"In the data centre, it takes six days to re-image a server typicallyassuming the backups are good," he says. If you have tens of thousands of servers, the cost and downtime associated with rolling back may be worse than paying the ransom.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Devising an incident response plan is a tall order for companies of any scale. A tabletop exercise is one of the best ways to prepare, and it's something any business can do. These exercises simulate a breach on paper and put your team's training and decision-making to the test. </p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"Go through the process and see where your capability gaps are because you're going to need to supplement those with third parties," explains Simonis.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>That may mean bringing in managed cybersecurity services for your entire system or filling gaps as needed with boutique solutions. The right third party can help with vulnerability assessment, unearthing harder to find gaps that might go unnoticed during your typical drills.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>"You've got to have those solutions established ahead of time because there's nothing worse than needing consulting and having to wait two or three weeks," Simonis says. "The reality of these breaches is that minutes and hours matter. The sooner you're able to investigate and eradicate, the sooner you're likely to have confidence that you've done it effectively."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="responding-and-recovering">Responding and recovering</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>According to Simonis, just about everyone has a planbut being able to put it into play is another story entirely. "People don't drill their plans. They don't practice their plans in a serious kind of way," he says. "[What is] more common than not having a plan [is] having a plan that is very dusty and doesn't actually work."<a href="https://www.hpe.com/content/hpe/country/us/en/discover-more-network.html?jumpid=in_510388602_dmnurl_nxtpgs053020"></a></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Simon Leech, the senior adviser for security and risk management at HPE Pointnext Services, adds that when it comes to incident responsewhether you've turned to a third party to help develop it or you're putting it in place yourself  the small details can make all the difference, right down to knowing exactly who to call at 2 a.m. with bad news.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Properly identifying what led to a breach, and making sure the hole is plugged, is crucial. "If you don't have a process in place to make sure you've contained the infection before you start cleaning things up and getting them back on the network, you're just going to be playing Whac-A-Mole, chasing down servers that keep getting reinfected," says Leech.</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p>Knowing what to do when your plan is testedand knowing what to do when your plan&nbsp;<em>fails</em>is just as important as having one in the first place, Simonis says, citing boxer Mike Tyson's famous quote, "Everyone has a plan until you get punched in the mouth."</p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->

<!-- wp:heading -->
<h2 id="security-incident-response-lessons-for-leaders">Security incident response: Lessons for leaders</h2>
<!-- /wp:heading -->

<!-- wp:list -->
<ul><li>Making a plan is just the first part. Putting it to the test with drills and tabletop exercises is a top priority. When you uncover capability gaps, fill them with third-party expertise.</li><li>Don't rely on backupsor the means to pay out in the event of a ransomware attack. For smaller businesses, these attacks can be fatal.</li><li>Stick to the fundamentals.</li></ul>
<!-- /wp:list -->

<!-- wp:paragraph -->
<p></p>
<!-- /wp:paragraph -->]]></content:encoded>
